President Roosevelt Orders Ban on Arms Shipments to Europe 19

Signs Declaration Implementing Neutrality Act, Does Not Apply to Canada and South Africa

Washington: President Roosevelt has recently ordered a ban on the shipment of arms to European belligerents. (Havas dispatch from the 6th)

Washington: The White House issued a public statement at 2:10 PM (New York time) stating that President Roosevelt has signed a declaration stating that the United States will maintain neutrality regarding the European war. Secretary of State Hull immediately announced it. (Havas dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: President Roosevelt signed a declaration at 6:30 PM regarding the European war, implementing the current Neutrality Act. (Havas dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: White House Secretary Early recently issued a statement, roughly saying that after the current Neutrality Act is announced for implementation by President Roosevelt, arms and various military supplies should be prohibited from being shipped to Europe. Americans traveling on ships of belligerent countries should also be restricted. The State Department has specially set up a department to be responsible for supervising the ban on arms and military supplies and is immediately preparing to start work. Department Director Green recently told a Havas reporter that he only needs to send a telegram to stop the shipment of arms to European belligerents. (Havas, 5th)

Washington: President Roosevelt and Secretary of State Hull have already signed a neutrality declaration, which immediately takes effect. According to President Roosevelt’s secretary Early, this declaration is based on international law and has nothing to do with the Neutrality Act. It is said that the declaration has more than 4,000 words in 17 articles, listing various things that Americans are not allowed to do, such as enlisting in foreign armies and donating military expenses. The second declaration made in accordance with the Neutrality Act is currently under consideration. (Reuter's dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: President Roosevelt announced yesterday that he would stop transporting arms and munitions to European belligerent countries. This afternoon, he issued a declaration on the implementation of the current Neutrality Act in the United States. This decision by the President to announce the Neutrality Act a few days after the outbreak of the European war was three and a half months earlier than President Wilson during the last war. The President stated in the declaration, "Germany and France, Poland, and the British Empire, including India, Australia, and New Zealand, are at war. The United States has decided not to participate." What is noteworthy in the declaration is that Canada is not listed. Canada has not yet officially declared war on Germany. This declaration will be effective immediately after being countersigned by Secretary of State Hull. The declaration lists 17 regulations that American citizens and foreigners must abide by within the United States. These regulations do not prohibit people from expressing sympathetic opinions, etc. President’s Secretary Early said that the government has not received any confirmed news of the discovery of submarines of unknown nationality in the Caribbean islands. Early went on to say that the so-called strict neutrality of the United States is not just about implementing the Neutrality Act, but will also make all departments work together to prevent the United States from being dragged into the whirlpool of war. Secretary of State Hull announced new regulations on Monday for American citizens traveling abroad, which require people to have proper documents proving that there are urgent matters when applying to the State Department for European travel passports. (Associated Press dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: The United States' declaration of maintaining neutrality regarding the European war was recently broadcast by national radio stations. This declaration does not apply to the Commonwealth of Canada and the Commonwealth of South Africa because they have not officially declared war on Germany, so they cannot be regarded as belligerent countries. According to the full text of the declaration, which is divided into 17 articles, in addition to the neutrality regulations in international law, it also stipulates that Americans shall not join the armies of various belligerent countries or hand over armed ships to various belligerent countries. No troops shall be trained in the United States to assist belligerent countries in combat. Warships of belligerent countries shall not obtain supplies in various ports in the United States. (Havas dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: People close to the White House recently stated that although President Roosevelt has signed a neutrality declaration regarding the European war and put the current Neutrality Act into effect, the government still hopes to make some changes or convene a temporary meeting of Congress in the short term to discuss the revision of the Neutrality Act. The key point is to abolish the clause in the current Neutrality Act that prohibits the shipment of arms to belligerent countries, because this clause is not only detrimental to Britain and France, but President Roosevelt also believes that it is psychologically and materially beneficial to Germany. Some say that several days have passed since the outbreak of the European war, and the reason why President Roosevelt has been slow to convene Congress is that he hopes that domestic public opinion can gradually agree with his views under the pressure of the European situation. This hope seems to have been realized, because according to reports, since the President delivered a speech on the 3rd of this month, stating that he would do everything possible to prevent the United States from being involved in the whirlpool of war, more and more Americans have agreed to abolish the current Neutrality Act. People in political circles also say that the majority of isolationist congressmen are now prepared to amend the Neutrality Act in accordance with the President's wishes. President Roosevelt especially hopes that the amendment he will propose in the future can be quickly passed by Congress without debate. (Havas dispatch from the 6th)

Ottawa: The Canadian government is still preparing to support its mother country in the war against Germany. However, since the United States announced its neutrality, there has been some speculation about the way Canada will assist its mother country. The United States' neutrality declaration lists the countries to which the United States prohibits the export of arms, but Canada is not included because Canada has not yet declared war on Germany. Therefore, in order for Canada to obtain materials, arms, and military raw materials from the United States, it is best not to declare war on Germany. If Canada does not take action as a belligerent country for one day, it can obtain materials from the United States for one day to supply the United States. This is actually better than sending troops to Europe to participate in the war. (Associated Press dispatch from the 6th)

British Ship "Athenia" Escapes Danger, Passengers Land in Succession 20

Still 257 People Missing, US Government Collects Facts and Evidence

Dublin: After the "Athenia" mail ship was sunk by a submarine, the ship's owner, Kirk, recently arrived here and told a Havas reporter, "The 'Athenia' was sunk by a torpedo. There is no doubt about that. One of the crew members personally saw the periscope of a submarine emerge from the sea just before the torpedo exploded. A few minutes later, a submarine surfaced and fired artillery shells at the 'Athenia'. Its goal was obviously to destroy the radio equipment." (Havas dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: After the British ship "Athenia" was sunk by a submarine, American passengers who were lucky enough to escape danger have landed successively in the ports of Glasgow, Scotland, and Galway, Ireland. US Ambassador to Britain Kennedy sent a naval attaché from the embassy to ask them about their experience of the accident. It is reported that they had personally seen the submarine launching the torpedo. Ambassador Kennedy has reported the results of the investigation to the State Department. However, it is still difficult to determine at this moment how many of the 311 American passengers were killed. The State Department is currently collecting various facts and intends to file a protest with the countries concerned based on them. (Havas dispatch from the 5th)

Glasgow: The Donaldson Line announced today that 257 of the 1,103 passengers and 315 crew members on its "Athenia," which was torpedoed on Sunday morning, are still missing. (Associated Press dispatch from the 6th)

Dublin: After the British mail ship "Athenia" was sunk by a submarine, 428 surviving passengers arrived at the port of Galway at noon today. Twelve of them were seriously injured, and there were many other injured people. According to a certain American student among the passengers, he was on the deck when the mail ship was sunk and witnessed the torpedo hitting the ship's hull. According to a ship's officer, the torpedo was launched from a distance of 800 to 1,000 yards. (Havas dispatch from the 5th)

London: After the British mail ship "Athenia" was sunk by a German submarine, the Labor Party's organ newspaper, the Daily Herald, reported that the ship was carrying a batch of gold worth £5 million, which was originally intended to be shipped to Canada and was said to have been recovered in full by the ships that went to rescue it. (Havas dispatch from the 6th)

London: Passengers who escaped from the British ship Athenia, which sank near Scotland, arrived at British ports last night. They told reporters that the ship did not receive a warning before being attacked by a submarine, and said that the submarine fired two artillery shells at the passengers in the lifeboats. Earl Stanhope stated in the House of Lords yesterday that there is no doubt that this unfortunate incident was caused by a submarine, and there were accurate reports from eyewitnesses that the submarine did not issue any warnings before carrying out the attack. However, news about the submarine firing artillery shells at passengers has not yet been officially confirmed. As for the exact number of deaths, it was still impossible to count yesterday. Earl Stanhope also believed that mines could not have caused the ship to sink, because "the ocean is unfathomably deep, and mines cannot be moored." According to those who were rescued, when passengers were climbing into lifeboats, a shell hit the deck of the "Athenia." According to a certain passenger, the second shell contained "poison gas." (Associated Press dispatch from the 5th)

Washington: The US government has begun collecting evidence to determine who should be held responsible for the sinking of the Athenia. The State Department announced that the US Minister to the Irish Free State telegraphed from Galway that he had met with the captain, crew, and American passengers of the Athenia. They all said that the Athenia was sunk by a submarine. (Reuter's dispatch from the 6th)

London: Of the 1,400 passengers on the British ship Athenia, which was sunk by a torpedo, 500 are still missing. Searches are continuing in all directions. The US consulate said that almost all of the 311 Americans have been rescued. None of the rescue ships have returned, and it is reported that the Southern Cross yacht has sailed directly to the United States. (Associated Press dispatch from the 6th)

United States Expands Naval Strength, Prevents Anti-American Activities 21

Washington: US President Roosevelt stated at a press conference yesterday that old US warships will also be put into naval service. In addition, the navy will be recruited to expand the size of the US Navy. At the same time, the strength of the Coast Guard and the garrison troops of the Panama Canal will also be increased. (Haitong dispatch from the 6th)

Washington: President Roosevelt recently announced that the government will take strict measures to stop anti-American movements in the country, and existing laws will be strictly enforced. (Haitong dispatch from the 6th)

Washington: US Chief of Naval Operations Leahy told the House Appropriations Committee that the US Navy Department is very interested in building and maintaining naval aircraft base facilities on Canton Island (a small Pacific island that both the United States and Britain claim to own). "If something happens in the Pacific, the island can be used as a base for our navy reconnaissance aircraft. Our country can use the island for Pacific exercises and study methods of mastering the environment. Building a naval aircraft base on Canton Island is an important task for the navy to defend the United States. The Navy Department is extremely interested in maintaining this facility. Britain and the United States competed for sovereignty over Canton Island, and later reached an understanding. Both sides enjoy equal rights on the island. Either side can use the island for various purposes, but it cannot prejudice the other party's sovereignty. Therefore, our country cannot allocate funds to turn the island into a naval aircraft base, and the government does not intend to make other improvements on the island at present, because our country has no right to exclusively enjoy the island." (Associated Press dispatch from the 6th)

Pan-American Conference Scheduled to be Held 22

Santiago, Chile: According to inquiries here, the foreign ministers of American countries are scheduled to meet in Panama on September 21. It is reported that this matter was initiated by the United States and Chile, and ten American countries will attend and participate. (Haitong dispatch from the 6th)

Washington: The Republic of Panama has invited American republics to participate in a conference of Latin American countries, the purpose of which is to maintain peace in the Western Hemisphere and prevent financial disturbances caused by the European war. (Reuter's dispatch from the 6th)

European Naval Vessel Changed to Return Home 23

Tokyo The European Naval Vessel has received orders to return home via the Panama Canal, instead of the Suez Canal. Vessels traveling between Europe and Japan will temporarily take the Mediterranean route. However, if the war spreads to the Mediterranean, ships traveling between Europe and Japan will use the Panama Canal. Due to the British naval blockade of the North Sea, European-bound vessels will now terminate in London instead of Hamburg. (Reuters, 6th)

European Gold Flows to America in Large Quantities 24

New York European gold is currently flowing into America in large quantities. The American mail steamer "President Roosevelt" recently arrived here, carrying 21 million gold dollars. The Cunard mail steamer "Samaria" also recently arrived with 15 million gold dollars. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

New York The British ship "Queen Mary" arrived here yesterday. In addition to carrying 2,331 passengers, it also carried gold worth 44.5 million gold dollars. Newspaper reports indicate that two British warships escorted the vessel as a precaution. (Haitong News Agency, 6th)

British Securities Market Reopens as Usual 25

Temporary Tea Prices Fixed, Foreigner Withdrawals Limited

London According to an official announcement, the stock market, which was closed last week due to the outbreak of war, is scheduled to reopen as usual tomorrow. Off-market securities trading has already begun, with prices higher than the closing prices of last Thursday. There were occasional transactions in industrial and oil stocks. The price of British government bonds has mostly risen slightly above the fixed minimum price. London gold and foreign exchange are all under government control. Gold transactions are entirely under the control of the Bank of England and are based on the bank's purchase price. Today, the Bank of England quoted gold at 168 shillings per ounce. The Bank of England yesterday set the exchange rate for the US dollar at $4.02 to $4.06. (Reuters, 6th)

London The British government today ordered temporary tea prices to be fixed and placed the wholesale and import trade of tea under government control. The government food department is now taking over all types of tea stored in the country's customs warehouses that have not yet been cleared, as well as those arriving in Britain in the future. According to this order, retail and wholesale prices may not exceed all prices within one week ending August 26. (Reuters, 5th)

Milan According to news received here, the British Treasury Department has stipulated that foreign nationals leaving Britain may only withdraw £25 from their bank deposits. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

Italy Quietly Awaits Developments, Can Join the War at Any Time 26

Rome Italy's neutrality is now more stable, as major shipping schedules are about to resume. However, Italian newspapers mostly insist that the country can join the war at any time. In addition, Mussolini's mouthpiece, "The Voice of Italy," published an editorial yesterday stating that the Italian people are now quietly awaiting "the development of the situation and Mussolini's orders," and that the Italian people's attitude is calm. "Their weapons have been placed at their feet, and their will has been forged to a strong degree by the flames of the Great Revolution and four wars. As for the reasons held by Britain, they will never change our minds." (Associated Press, 5th)

German Farmers and Workers Do Not Want War 27

London The British Independent Labour Party today received a letter from members of the German Independent Social Democratic Party, sent on the eve of the war, stating that German farmers and workers do not want war, and that while they love their country, they do not share the same views as the current regime. "We have opposed Austria's occupation, the annexation of Czechoslovakia, and Hitler's policies of aggression and war in leaflets. Even workers in forts under the surveillance of secret detectives have these leaflets. This war is not our war. In the face of death and destruction, please do not forget us and the ideas for which we die by cruel punishment or in concentration camp suffering. We, like you, love our country, but our common homeland is humanity." (Reuters, 5th)

German Envoy to Iraq Lowers Flag and Returns Home 28

Capital of Iraq The government has decided to sever diplomatic relations with Germany. The German envoy to Iraq, Mr. Krobba, lowered the flag and returned home at noon today. (Havas, 6th)

Germany and Finland Conduct Business Negotiations 29

Capital of Finland German envoy Mr. Haisell arrived here yesterday to conduct business talks with Finland. He immediately visited Minister of State Mr. Kajander, Finance Minister Tanner, and Foreign Minister Öko. Mr. Haisell expressed the German government's desire to continue developing German-Finnish business relations based on the current foundation under extraordinary circumstances. He stated that if there are difficulties, they should be resolved through friendly negotiations. The Finnish ministers solemnly declared Finland's absolute neutrality and the Finnish government's desire to maintain free business relations. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

United States Restricts Cotton Imports 30

Washington President Roosevelt, adopting the recommendations of the Tariff Commission, announced today restrictions on the import of raw cotton and waste cotton in order to protect the American market. (Reuters, 5th)

Washington The International Cotton Congress today adjourned until Saturday after listening to the opening speech of U.S. Secretary of Agriculture Wallace. According to the views of U.S. officials, the current international situation makes the meeting unlikely to succeed. Representatives from nine countries came to the United States to attend this Cotton Congress, including India, Egypt, Brazil, Britain, France, the Soviet Union, Peru, Sudan, and Mexico. The U.S. Secretary of Agriculture stated at the congress that the European war has made the problem of disposing of surplus cotton in the United States even more difficult. According to his opinion, the military use of cotton has increased, while ordinary uses have decreased. The two offset each other, but the increase is not as great as the decrease. (Reuters, 5th)

Japanese Foreign Ministry Reiterates Neutrality Toward European War, Advises Britain and France to Withdraw Naval and Military Forces in China 31

Tokyo The Japanese Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs yesterday informed the ambassadors to Japan from Britain, Germany, France, Poland, and Italy, declaring Japan's attitude of non-interference in the European war, with wording similar to that of the new Prime Minister General Abe the previous day. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

Tokyo The Japanese government yesterday requested the governments of Britain and France to "voluntarily" withdraw naval and military forces stationed in China, in order to avoid unexpected incidents as a result of the European war. The request was made yesterday when the British and French ambassadors to Japan visited the Foreign Ministry. There was no indication here of how the British and French governments would respond to the request. The Japanese side solemnly stated that Japan's request was a "suggestion" rather than a demand. (Associated Press, 6th)

Tokyo It is reported that the Japanese government has suggested to the diplomatic representatives of Britain, France, Poland, and Germany to withdraw their military forces stationed in China in order to avoid unexpected incidents. It is reported that when British Ambassador Craig accepted this suggestion, he stated that there were no German troops stationed within China, so there was no possibility of conflict. However, the British Ambassador will report the matter to the Foreign Office in London for final decision. (Reuters, 6th)

Tokyo The Cabinet held an emergency meeting this morning to discuss the European situation based on information provided by Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Abe, and exchanged views on possible future developments. Minister of War Hata Shunroku reported that fighting in the Nomonhan region had subsided in the past few days. After the meeting, Abe entered the palace to report to the Emperor on domestic and foreign affairs. (Reuters, 6th)

Washington The Japanese government has followed the policies of the United States and the Soviet Union and declared non-interference in the European war. There are two factors in Japan's declaration of neutrality: (1) The conclusion of the German-Soviet non-aggression pact allows the Soviet Union to act freely in the Far East. (2) Japan is preoccupied with its war in China. Observers believe that Japan's current decision on the European war is similar to that of the First World War, because Japan was then allied with Britain. Therefore, some believe that the evolution of the European war may allow Britain and Japan to relive their old alliance dream, and Japan can now seize the markets of Britain, Germany, and France in the Far East. Others say that Japan will take the opportunity to improve relations with the United States, but at present, there is no optimistic hope for this. As for the European war's impact on China, some believe that it will affect China's source of military supplies, but in fact, China's military supplies can already be self-sufficient, and China's coast has long been blockaded by Japan, so the outbreak of the European war will not have an impact on self-sufficient China. (Associated Press, 6th)

Tokyo When foreign reporters asked the spokesman of the Japanese Foreign Ministry what the significance of Japan's declaration of neutrality was, the spokesman replied, "This declaration does not indicate the meaning of neutrality in international law. Japan only expresses its unwillingness to be involved in the whirlpool of the European war." When asked if this could be interpreted as conditional neutrality, the spokesman avoided the question. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

Moscow Yesterday, Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov and Japanese Ambassador to the Soviet Union held a long conversation, and planned to discuss a solution to the disputes and outstanding issues in Manchuria and Mongolia. Political circles here believe that this conversation is of considerable significance. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

Tokyo The spokesman of the Japanese Foreign Ministry stated today that he believes that Japanese Ambassador to the Soviet Union Togo Shigenori has conducted negotiations with Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov in an attempt to resolve the disputes in Manchuria and Mongolia. The spokesman said that Togo did not receive instructions from Tokyo to conduct these negotiations. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

Japanese Sources Report Mongolian Border Situation, Hailar Implements Air Defense

Tokyo According to Japanese frontline sources received here today, fighting in the Nomonhan region has subsided since September 2. Soviet-Mongolian mechanized units, numbering three divisions, that crossed the border north of the Balshagal Heights and south of the Nord Heights have been blocked by the Japanese-"Manchukuo" allied forces and cannot advance. The Japanese army previously discovered that more than 250 Soviet tanks were blocked and abandoned. On Sunday, Japanese aircraft engaged 80 enemy aircraft in the border airspace, shooting down 22 of them, while one Japanese aircraft was lost. (Reuters, 6th)

Hailar Colonel Shiraki, Deputy Commander of the Japanese Army in the Nomonhan area, recently told an Associated Press reporter, "The Japanese army is willing to engage in large-scale conflict with the Soviet troops. It is quite difficult to deal with small teams of Soviet troops that sneak across at night, so we are willing to fight the other side in a decisive battle and will not be afraid." Hailar has implemented a blackout, with the entire city dark after 8:30 pm every night. In addition, the trains arriving here every night are full of Japanese troops, and the windows on the train are covered with black curtains 300 miles from the city to prevent light from leaking. At this time, passengers are strictly prohibited from peeking out the windows. (Associated Press, 6th)

Soviet People Support Government Policy 32

Moscow After the Fourth Extraordinary Session of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union closed, mass meetings were held throughout the country to discuss it. The result of the meetings in Moscow, Leningrad, Stalingrad, Kharkov, Saratov, Almaty and other cities was that the entire working masses unanimously expressed their firm support for all resolutions of the session. (TASS, 5th)

Germany and Soviet Union Hold Military Talks, Italian Military Observation Group to Visit Berlin Shortly 33

Berlin Reliable sources say that the Soviet plenipotentiary military attache held several talks here today with senior German military officers. The same sources claim that an Italian military observation group could arrive here this week. (Associated Press, 6th)

France Establishes Information Office, Emphasizes Propaganda 34

Paris The Director of the Information Office recently made a radio broadcast to the nation, stating: "The Director of the Information Office hereby announces to all male and female citizens of the country that this office has been established and is responsible for reporting the war situation. However, this matter is of great importance, and I am well aware of the country's thirst for news. But news concerning military strategy, except for those that do not hinder our military actions or are not enough to facilitate the enemy's army, are difficult to publish. I hope the people of the country understand this. As for the current time, it is actually a period of preparation for the great war, and no incidents have occurred on our country's border. The details of the military concentration or mobilization situation are also inconvenient to report. I am happy to inform you that General Gamelin, the Commander-in-Chief, believes that all situations are extremely appropriate. As of today, the civilized world has issued its final call, and our country's people are able to understand this and are willing to respond at the cost of sacrifice, which is greatly appreciated. For this reason, I also wish to be frank and disclose as much as possible and explain as much as possible, except for those that would harm French interests. I would like to mention that in the future, there may be situations where it is necessary to temporarily maintain silence due to the damage of broadcasting equipment or the obstruction of news sources. However, it is not desirable for the people of the country to be separated from the facts, that is, to be separated from the soldiers on the front lines. As for why I do not talk about Italy, it is because there is nothing to talk about. The reason why I do not talk about the British army is because the British army has already mobilized, the same as our country, so it is inconvenient to comment. As for the British Navy, it has already passed the mobilization stage, which I believe is well known to the people of the country. The war reports published by our General Headquarters may seem too brief and dull to the people of the country, but their true value can be understood by comparing them with the war reports of the early 1914. During 1914, our group was attacked while working and was somewhat flustered. At this time, our country has offensive and defensive weapons, and the border defense line is as solid as gold, so we can maintain calm and do not need to say much. This is the difference between now and then. Britain and France are now united and working together. Although the enemy country is extremely powerful, judging from historical precedents, it will undoubtedly be defeated. When reading war reports, I hope you will understand this intention." (Havas, 5th)

France and Poland Sign Mutual Assistance Agreement, Stipulating the Obligation of Mutual Assistance, Signatory Countries May Not Conclude Peace Separately 35

Paris Foreign Minister Bonnet recently signed a protocol with Polish Ambassador Lukasiewicz, stipulating mutual assistance obligations. The relationship maintained by Britain and France with Poland is absolutely the same from now on. (Note: Britain and Poland signed a mutual assistance agreement on the 25th of last month.) The preamble to the protocol states that when one signatory country is attacked by a third country, the other signatory country has an obligation to provide assistance. This obligation is based on the current alliance treaties between France and Poland. The main text of the protocol is divided into five articles, and the contents are as follows: (1) The signatory countries shall provide mutual assistance when either signatory country is attacked by a third country. If the independence of one signatory country is threatened directly or indirectly by another European country, and therefore has to use force to resist, the other signatory country shall also provide assistance. (2) The method of implementing the mutual assistance obligations of the signatory countries shall be determined jointly by the military authorities of both parties. (3) The signatory countries shall notify each other of the anti-aggression agreements concluded with third countries. If either signatory country intends to conclude such agreements with other countries in the future, it shall also notify the other signatory country. However, the mutual assistance obligations stipulated in this protocol shall not be changed due to other agreements of either signatory country. (4) If the signatory countries join the war, they may not conclude peace separately or conclude an armistice agreement separately. (5) The effective period of this protocol is the same as the current alliance treaties between France and Poland in 1921. (Havas, 5th)

Paris Diplomatic circles here recently commented on the mutual assistance relationship between Britain, France and Poland, saying that each country promises not to conclude peace separately or conclude an armistice agreement separately. In other words, after the outbreak of war, neither Britain nor France may compromise with Germany without the consent of the Polish government, and Poland may not sign a peace agreement with Germany when the allied countries continue to fight. The steps are clear, and the meaning is very significant. Someone who recently returned from Germany claimed that Germany generally believed that neither Britain nor France were willing to help Poland. The German people were quite surprised to learn that Britain had intervened. It was only two days after France declared a state of war that the German authorities made it public to the people. According to Hitler's original plan, he would first defeat Poland and then turn to deal with the Western European countries, so that those countries would know that even if they wanted to help Poland, it would be too late. (Havas, 6th)

British and French Ambassadors to Germany Return Safely 36

Woerden, Netherlands British Ambassador to Germany Henderson and his staff crossed the German-Dutch border this afternoon. The British Ambassador and others had been waiting in German territory since dawn for news that the staff of the German Embassy in Britain had safely arrived in Dutch territorial waters, as the German government would not allow the British Ambassador and others to leave the country until the staff of the German Embassy had been released by Britain. The Dutch government mediated, and the exchange procedures for the ambassadors of the two countries were completed today. (Reuters, 5th)

Paris French Ambassador to Germany Coulondre arrived here by special train from Belgium at 5:15 pm today. He immediately went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to report everything. The embassy staff have all returned home with him. (Havas, 5th)

Amsterdam All the staff of the British and French embassies in Germany exchanged withdrawals with all the staff of the German embassies in Britain and France yesterday in Oldenzaal. Yesterday morning, France specially opened a train to carry the staff of the German embassy to Oldenzaal. German Ambassador to France Weizsäcker led his subordinates to transfer to German vehicles and return to Beijing. French Ambassador to Germany Coulondre also led his subordinates to transfer to French vehicles and returned to Paris immediately. Yesterday afternoon, Britain and Germany also exchanged embassy staff in Oldenzaal. British Ambassador Henderson led his subordinates back home, and German Charge d'Affaires Guter led his subordinates from Oldenzaal by car back to Berlin. (Haitong Telegraph, 6th)

Smuts Succeeds as Prime Minister of South Africa, One Person Holds Three Key Positions, New Zealand Has Declared War 37

Cape Town The new South African cabinet will be headed by General Smuts as Prime Minister, concurrently in charge of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Defense. Hofmeyr will serve as Minister of Finance and Education. The opposition party will be part of the former Prime Minister Hertzog government. In view of the above situation, it can be seen that the South African government is now led by General Smuts, who is doing his best to support Britain. Smuts once led troops in British East Africa during the last great war. As for former government leader Hertzog, he did not advocate declaring support for Britain, but suggested that South Africa should maintain the same relationship with the Entente and Germany. (Reuters, 6th)

London After the South African Federation severed diplomatic relations with Germany, diplomatic circles here commented that the move was extremely important, as Britain could obtain great assistance from South Africa, and the South African Federation was one of the most unrestrained outside of the British Empire's dominions. In the past, when enemies of Britain attempted to leave the dominions, they often targeted the South African Federation. This resolute support for Britain is reassuring. (Havas, 6th)

London The New Zealand Dominion Parliament unanimously passed a resolution this afternoon approving the declaration of war against Germany. (Havas, 5th)

London The King and Queen of England set off by car from Buckingham Palace last night to inspect the civil defense forces. This was the first time the King and Queen had appeared in public since the outbreak of war on September 3. (Reuters, 6th)

Beijing After the Belgian government was reorganized on Sunday to include the Socialist Party in the cabinet, it has now reaffirmed its determination to maintain Belgium's neutrality. The policy statement submitted to the Chamber of Representatives yesterday stated that Belgium seeks peace, but its desire to seek peace is not only out of its own interests, but also based on emotions and human solidarity, so its efforts to avoid catastrophes do not make Belgium indifferent to everything. The statement asked the House of Representatives to immediately pass a number of special proposals, and stated that the entire Belgian army is now ready to fulfill its responsibilities under the command of the King of Belgium. (Reuters, 6th)

Aachen, Germany, Was Attacked by Air Raid Yesterday 38

Brussels Aachen, an important city in Prussia (forty miles southwest of Cologne), was reportedly bombed yesterday. According to a dispatch from the Paris Evening News, sirens and explosions were heard in many places on the Belgian border. (Reuters, 6th)

German War Report, Freight Transportation in East Prussia Resumes 39

Berlin The semi-official German News Agency recently issued news of yesterday's war, saying that the German troops fighting in Poland are now advancing step by step according to the original plan. The combat situation of the various armies is divided as follows: (1) Our mountain army and other troops have occupied the northern slope of the Beskid Mountains and are attacking Nowy Sącz. (2) The enemy is retreating towards Kraków, and our forces are approaching the city from the southwest. (3) After occupying the eastern industrial area of Upper Silesia Province, our army captured the enemy positions on the Cieszyn-Jablunkov-Bielsko-Biała line in one fell swoop yesterday afternoon. (4) On the front line of Sieradz, our troops have broken through the enemy positions and are now advancing towards Łódź along the east bank of the Warta River. (5) The enemy troops on the front lines of the east bank of the Vistula River and Kutno have begun to retreat and are being pursued by our army. (6) Our army, which attacked Poland from East Prussia, has captured Ciechanów, and the enemy troops are retreating to the south. (7) Our mechanized units will attack Narew. As of now, our northern army has captured 10,000 enemy troops and seized 60 artillery pieces. (8) Our air force destroyed many enemy joint lines and various transportation facilities yesterday. The train stations in Tczew, Walda, Skarszewy, Darlów, and Frekin were hit and burned, and many railway lines were cut off. (9) Enemy aircraft have never invaded our airspace, and few have been seen except for a few interceptors. (10) Our warships sank another enemy submarine in the Baltic Sea yesterday. So far, this is the third enemy submarine destroyed by our warships. (Havas, 6th)

President of the Executive Yuan Kong Expresses Opinions on the Current Situation; The European Situation Has No Adverse Impact on the War of Resistance; The Entire Nation Should Be More Vigilant and Strive Harder 49

Chongqing: Since the outbreak of the European war, all parties have been quite concerned about the evolution of the European situation and its impact on the future of China's war of resistance. Yesterday, a reporter visited President Kong of the Executive Yuan somewhere and asked for his views on the current situation. He graciously gave the following statement: Our Chinese nation is a nation that deeply loves peace. Maintaining harmonious relations with our neighbors is a consistent foreign policy of the National Government. Therefore, in dealing with neighboring countries, we have spared no effort and shown the greatest patience in seeking ways to achieve peace. However, the peace we refer to is an equal, honorable, and genuine peace. As for those who attempt to force us into humiliating surrender through violent aggression, we will not hesitate to resist with the greatest determination and the greatest sacrifice. If the Japanese militarists fantasize about destroying our country and then invading the world, then the only way we can deal with them is to resist to the end, until the Japanese thoroughly abandon their policy of aggression. As for the Japanese's constant rumors and slanders, this is their consistent tactic of sowing discord and is not worth a smile from the knowledgeable. Now, unfortunately, the European war has broken out. Standing on the position of world peace and the well-being of mankind, we can only deeply regret it. I firmly believe that the European war has no adverse impact on the future of our war of resistance. Moreover, since the purpose of our war of resistance is to fight for national independence and freedom, and to safeguard world justice and peace, this purpose cannot be stopped for a single day until it is achieved. However, the Japanese militarists may take advantage of the situation to intensify their violent acts, so our responsibility for resisting aggression and maintaining stability in the Far East will be doubled compared to the past. Therefore, at this moment, the entire nation should be more vigilant and strive harder, and under the leadership of Chairman Chiang, make redoubled efforts. The reporter then inquired about the recent situation of China's finance and economy. Mr. Kong replied with a pleasant expression, "You also know that the recent foreign exchange situation has slightly improved, and that the market price of public bonds has risen uniformly. It must be known that the changes in foreign exchange and the bond market are always faster and more pronounced in wartime than in peacetime, and the related factors are also very complex. The rise and fall of foreign exchange are indeed important, but such phenomena have no significant impact on the effectiveness of our legal tender in the country. We should not be overly pleased with the occasional rise in foreign exchange, nor should we be overly anxious about its decline. What should be paid attention to now is the domestic price level, and the price of food is the most important. Fortunately, our country's agricultural production has had another bumper harvest this year. The government's current problem is how to avoid low grain prices hurting farmers. Except for a very small number of cities, there is no worry about excessively high grain prices. This is enough to prove that ordinary economic theories are often not suitable for China's national conditions. China's finance and economy have entered the right track and their strength has gradually increased since the successive reorganizations in recent years. For more than two years of the war of resistance, thanks to the wise leadership of the leader and the enthusiastic maintenance of the people of the whole country, it has been able to be maintained until now and stands firm, which is something to be thankful for. In the future, we must respond to all changes in finance and economy with a calm and cautious attitude, and I believe that we will be able to overcome all kinds of difficulties and fulfill the mission of wartime finance. If the people of the whole country trust the government, obey the leader, and deal with things calmly, it will be of great help to the future of the country." (Dispatch of the 6th)

Two Million People in Tianjin Threatened by Famine 55

Tianjin: Two million people in Tianjin are threatened by famine due to the great flood. The flood is extremely severe, unprecedented in decades. Not only Tianjin city itself was flooded, but the surrounding villages within 50 miles have also become a watery expanse. The farmland and vegetable gardens on which Tianjin's food supply depends have all been washed away by the flood. Foreign commercial firms in the British and French concessions have suffered huge losses. In several places in the concessions, the water depth is as much as nine feet. At present, all commerce in Tianjin has been suspended. Electricity and telephone services in the concessions have been interrupted. The goods stored in the warehouses have been severely damaged, and the foundations of many houses have been destroyed. Newspapers have stopped publishing, and merchants have closed their businesses. Only a few hardy Chinese are trying to sell goods by rowing rafts. The only means of transportation in the city is boats. In places where the water is three feet deep, there are still a few rickshaws carrying passengers, but the fares are extremely expensive. Even for a very short distance, it costs silver dollars, and passengers have to sit on the hood of the rickshaw, placing their feet where the seats originally were, in order to avoid water immersion. A few Chinese who have boats are making a lot of profit, with short-distance fares as high as twenty yuan. The warehouses, tall buildings, and rooftops are now occupied by refugees. The accumulated water is becoming increasingly polluted, leading to an increase in cholera and skin diseases. In addition, with the rupture of many cesspools, the entire city is filled with a foul smell. It is heard that the Japanese suffered the greatest blow in the Tianjin flood. Not only has the thriving import business completely stopped, but also their ambitious construction plans in North China will be delayed for several months. (Special dispatch from Reuters)

Changzhi and Changzi in Shanxi Still Under Chinese Siege 56

Luoyang: Changzhi and Changzi in southeastern Shanxi are still under siege by the Chinese troops. There are more than 1,000 Japanese troops each in Xiadian, Qitingzhen, Qin County, and Zhangyuanzhen, and they are heavily guarding the highways. After Tunliu was recovered by the Chinese troops, more than 1,000 remaining Japanese troops collapsed and fled to Wangcun, Lucun, and Changcunzhen (all northeast of Tunliu). A Chinese unit is still engaged in fierce fighting with the Japanese troops. (Dispatch of the 6th)

Xi'an: More than 5,000 Japanese troops who crossed the Fen River to the west attacked Jundu on the morning of the 5th, and a fierce battle is underway. The Japanese are also firing artillery shells at the west bank of the Chinese side, and the Chinese artillery is also aiming and returning fire. (Dispatch of the 6th)

Chaoshan Chinese Troops Recapture Half of the Chaoshan Railway; Japanese Troops in Caitang City Suffer a Major Defeat; Japanese Troops Attempt to Defend Chao'an 57

Shantou correspondent: The Wu Qiwai unit of the 　　　Army Group launched a three-pronged counter-offensive on Chaoshan. Starting on August 23rd, they advanced sharply along the Chaoshan Railway line. The Chinese and Japanese troops immediately began to engage in battle. On the morning of the 24th, the Chinese Air Force flew from a certain location to Chaoshan and bombed the Japanese strongholds on Zhugaoshan, Hulushan, and Bijia Mountain in Chao City, and disseminated a letter from the Director of the 　　　Army Group and the Pacification Commissioner of the Fujian, Guangdong, and Jiangxi Border Region to the people of Dongjiang, urging the people to use the unique revolutionary spirit of Guangdong to "abide by government laws and decrees, firmly believe that the War of Resistance will be victorious and the nation will be built, assist the army, defend their hometowns, and implement the twelve articles of the National Covenant. Everyone must be able to memorize them, write them out one by one, and earnestly implement the covenant, encouraging each other," etc.

On the 23rd, the Hua Zhenzhong Brigade of the Chinese army departed from east of Sangpu and recaptured the Hailian Mountain position near Pengzhou. Another team was dispatched to pursue the Japanese troops. On the morning of the 24th, they had advanced to Hong'an Township near Caitang, completing the encirclement line. Caitang City is the central station of the Chaoshan Railway. The Japanese troops occupied this station to maintain the Chaoshan land communication line and stationed 300 to 500 soldiers in Anbu, Huamei, Wuyang, Fuyang, Fengxi, and Chao'an, each with a commander and built solid defensive works. The Chinese troops set up strongholds along the foothills of Sangpu Mountain, relying on the mountain's terrain to build defenses. The outpost of the Chinese side was located five miles from the railway line. Before dawn on the 25th, the Chinese troops launched an attack on Caitang City in three directions, surprising the Japanese troops and breaking into the Japanese positions. The Japanese troops retreated in a panic to the pre-built defensive positions in the city. The Chinese troops then launched a fierce attack on the Japanese troops with concentrated artillery fire. At this time, the firepower of both sides was equal, and the sounds of guns and cannons were completely consistent, making it impossible to distinguish which side was firing. After three hours of fierce fighting, the Kurokawa unit of the Japanese army was defeated and fled north along the railway line to Guanchao. The Chinese troops pursued closely, and the Japanese troops abandoned guns, cannons, and ammunition on the side of the road. Even the military supplies stored in the workers' quarters at Caitang Station were seized by the Chinese troops and carried up Sangpu Mountain. The Japanese troops stationed in Guanchao and Jinshihu heard that the Japanese troops in Caitang City had suffered a major defeat and dispatched 500 to 600 soldiers to cover the retreat of the defeated troops to Chao'an and block the pursuing Chinese troops. From noon onwards, under the scorching sun, the two sides engaged in five fierce hand-to-hand battles in the orange groves. All the orange groves were trampled into flat ground. Six Japanese aircraft flew in to drop bombs and fire guns. The Chinese troops, with no cover in the fields, were forced to disperse and fought the Japanese troops in groups of two or three. After another night of fighting, the guns and cannons fell silent on the morning of the 26th. The scattered Chinese troops returned to Sangpu Mountain and guarded the heights around Hailian Mountain. In this battle, more than 200 Japanese troops were killed, and a large number of military supplies were seized. They are now being inventoried and distributed to the various local militia teams.

When the Chinese troops attacked Caitang on the 23rd, they also dispatched another force to attack Jiaoshan Township at Huamei Station in order to prevent the Japanese troops from raiding the rear of the Chinese troops from Shantou and Anbu. The Japanese troops only set up a sentry post with about 30 sentries there. When they saw the Chinese troops approaching, they did not dare to engage in battle and fled to the Zhuanglong of Anbu. At noon on the 24th, about 300 Japanese troops from Anbu attacked Xiaowei Shen by land and water in two directions. The Chinese troops launched a joint attack with the local militia. The river channel there is extremely winding, and the Japanese troops were advancing in depth by motorboat, when they were blocked by a stone bridge and ambushed by ambush soldiers on the shore. Two motorboats were sunk. The Japanese soldiers scrambled ashore but did not know the way forward or backward, and many drowned in the water. There were 40 to 50 floating corpses. The Chinese troops captured about 40 to 50 rifles. When the Japanese soldiers were defeated and fled, they arrested villagers along the way to lead the way and set fire to civilian houses to vent their anger. Since the 28th, the central section of the Chaoshan Railway, from Huamei Station to Caitang, Wuyang, and Fuyang Stations, has been in the hands of the Chinese troops, occupying half of the entire line. Local militiamen are being hired to speed up the dismantling of the rails and sleepers. Two months of construction by the Japanese side have been completely wasted. In addition, the Japanese side forced each township to send out militiamen to form road protection teams last month. If the track was damaged, the nearby townships were responsible for repairing it. Now that it has all been dismantled, the townships no longer have to bear this heavy responsibility.

The Japanese troops entrenched in Chao City are very frightened because of the advance of the Chinese troops from all directions. They have cut off traffic, checked household registration, and only allowed residents to enter and exit. They have also arrested men under the age of 50 and sent them to the suburbs to step up the construction of defensive works. More than ten strongholds have been added on the opposite bank of the East Gate, from the foot of Bijia Mountain to the Jianjin gate, with obstacles and barbed wire arranged. The interior walls of the shops and houses in the streets and alleys of the city have all been dug through. The four city gates and key points are strictly searched for pedestrians, and many small alleys and streets have been sealed off, preparing for street fighting. There are 800 Japanese troops inside the city, and more outside the city. There are 300 at Yixi Station, and 500 each stationed on Zhugaoshan, Hulusuan, and Bijia Mountain. More than 30 motorboats and 200 other civilian boats are moored at Xiangzi Bridge. The motorboats patrol the river. The large army of the Chinese side, departing from Anjie Road and Tiandongxu, is about ten miles away from the city, and small units have dispersed and besieged various points in the suburbs. The sound of artillery fire is heard in the city every day. The date of the capture of the city is not far away.

Wuxi Chinese Troops Attack Japanese Troops at Night; Traffic on the Wuxi-Yixing Highway Interrupted 58

Wuxi correspondent: The Chinese troops in the four townships have been unusually active recently. At about 11:00 PM on August 28th, Zhou Hanliang, the commander of the Special Service Brigade of the West District of the Wuxi Anti-Enemy Self-Defense Corps, led the First Company and the Anti-Traitor Corps to attack the Japanese headquarters in the Xiexin Woolen Mill in Wuhebang, outside the North Gate, at night. The battle lasted for an hour. Because it was late at night, the casualties of the Japanese troops were unknown. They also set fire to and destroyed hundreds of boxes of Japanese military gasoline and several houses before returning safely. Also, a section of the Xiyi Highway from Rongxiang to Yangwan, totaling six miles, was destroyed by the team the day before. Therefore, traffic between Wuxi and Yixing was interrupted. Also, the notorious traitor Hu Jugen repeatedly led Japanese troops to harass the countryside. He was also shot and killed by the Anti-Traitor Corps in the Beitang opium smoking den the other day. It was in broad daylight, and it was located in the busy market street of Beikuang, so the traitors were very apprehensive.

Japanese Troops Plunder the Fisheries of the Zhoushan Islands; A Puppet Fisheries Administration is Established 59

Dinghai correspondent: The Zhoushan Islands in eastern Zhejiang are the largest fishing grounds in China. More than 200,000 fishermen make a living from this. The annual fish production reaches 20 million yuan in national currency. Among them, yellow croaker, cuttlefish, and ribbonfish are the most important, and they are sold to various parts of the country.

Since the fall of Dinghai County in the Zhoushan Islands, the Japanese troops have successively occupied Daishan Island and Shenjiamen Town, the centers of the fishing industry. They have wooed Gao Asheng and Zhou Jimei, scoundrels in the fishing industry, to come forward and organize the so-called "Fisheries Administration" and do everything possible to control and monopolize it. The "Administration" has also formulated regulations, forcing fishermen to register and charging so-called "registration fees" of 2 yuan, 5 yuan, 10 yuan, and even 50 yuan, depending on the size of the fishing boat. It has also assigned numbers to all fishing boats and issued a flag and a Japanese army flag, forcing them to be hung at the bow of each boat.

Recently, the Japanese troops have hired several large and small steamships, named "Huazhong Maru," to transport the fish products of the islands to the Shanghai "Fish Market" for sale and prohibit fishermen from transporting fish products to non-Japanese-occupied areas. A Japanese warship has now been dispatched to anchor in the Jintang waters between Dinghai and Ningbo. Whenever ice-cold ships carrying fish pass through that area, they are intercepted and set on fire.

The provincial-run Senior Aquatic Products School and a large-scale ice-making plant and cold storage, originally established in Dinghai, have made great achievements in improving the fishing industry. Since the Japanese troops entered the city, they have forcibly occupied the school and turned it into a hospital for wounded soldiers. They have also turned the ice-making plant into an ice-making company and sold artificial ice to fishermen at high prices.

Shandong Chinese Troops Recapture Pingdu, Zhaoyuan, and Yexian; Japanese Troops Are Threatened and Will Retreat to Qingdao When They Can No Longer Hold Out 60

Qingdao correspondent: The Chinese troops in the Jiaodong area have now launched a large-scale guerrilla war. Local militias have also risen up in succession, waving their spears and launching attacks in coordination with the Chinese army. A few days ago, the army and civilians jointly attacked Pingdu County. The Japanese troops defending the city were caught by surprise by the Chinese army's attacks from all sides. Their mechanical weapons failed to deploy. The Chinese army then selected a brave team to climb the city walls and join the local populace in a coordinated attack from within. At that time, they seized the key positions at each city gate and erected dozens of light machine guns on the city walls to sweep the Japanese positions. More than 200 Japanese and puppet troops in the city engaged in a fierce battle with the Chinese army for a day and a night. The civilian houses they occupied were also set on fire by the Chinese army. The Japanese and puppet troops suffered heavy casualties. Except for a few who jumped off the city walls and fled, the rest were almost completely annihilated. Pingdu County was officially recovered by the Chinese army and civilians, and a large number of military supplies and weapons were seized. The Japanese troops in Zhaoyuan and Yexian have been severely threatened and are in a state of panic. The Japanese Command in Qingdao issued an order to transfer the Japanese defense forces on the Jiaoji Railway Line, concentrated in Gaomi and Jiaoxian, and dispatched more than 60 trucks to advance to Fangzitingkou, intending to counterattack Pingdu. However, the Chinese army and civilians in Jiaodong have taken strict precautions and completely destroyed the highway from Shan Gao Mi to Pingdu, cutting dozens of ditches, so that the Japanese trucks and soldiers could not pass. When the Chinese army recovered Pingdu, it also seized an order from the Japanese Commander Akiyama to Gao Yupu, the commander of the 5th Brigade of the puppet 4th Route Army in Yexian. The main points are: (1) Yu Xuezhong's and Xu Xiangqian's troops are launching a major counterattack in southern Shandong, and they are engaged in fierce battles every day; (2) Zhang Buyun's troops are gathering in Zhucheng to Gaomi; (3) If the situation in Jiaodong is tense and they cannot hold out, each unit can retreat to Qingdao and concentrate there. In this situation, the Japanese troops in Jiaodong are showing signs of wavering.

Commercial News

Finance Frequent Unfavorable News; Gold Buying Resurges 61

Chips Suddenly Feel Insufficient; Peak Reaches Four Thousand Yuan

Yesterday, the situation in the spot gold market continued to rise sharply, the surge was very strong, and as a result, it leaped up another 415 yuan. However, the fluctuations in the middle were still quite rapid, often fluctuating around 100 yuan. However, most people, especially non-industry retail investors, have a bullish psychological view. This is because of the recent agreement between Japan and the Soviet Union, and the concessions made by both Britain and Japan, so everyone fears that there may be unfavorable effects on China, so there are quite a few people who absorb on dips, which is the opposite of the situation last weekend and Monday. The overall potential throughout the day was generally a sharp rise first, followed by a sharp fall, and then a rise again. At the beginning, the remaining momentum from the previous day did not subside. In addition, the foreign exchange rate was tight, and people's hearts became more firm, resulting in a rush of buyers. The opening in the morning was as high as 3,800 yuan, and then it soared to 3,850 yuan. Later, because a certain gold firm (acting for out-of-town customers) and silver firms threw in their chips, it once fell back to a low of 3,750 yuan. Subsequently, due to tighter foreign exchange and the strong advances of a certain bank on behalf of outsiders, and the continued strong absorption by a certain gold firm, the position suddenly felt more demand than supply, and the market jumped straight up again, breaking the 4,000 yuan mark, reaching a peak of 4,020 yuan. However, before long, as foreign exchange eased, the idea of ​​floating more profits emerged spontaneously. At that time, a certain gold firm once again helped out-of-town customers with a lot of selling, which led to a sharp turn downward, plummeting to 3,810 yuan. The noon close then rebounded to 3,840 yuan. In the afternoon, a certain bank's buying became strong again, rising to 3,940 yuan, and then suddenly fell to 3,850 yuan. However, the result was a closing price of 3,895 yuan, with active trading, still around 2,000 taels. Silver jewelry finally followed suit and increased by 45 yuan. The customs gold and the buying price of Chinese cash were all rising sharply in unison.

Spot Gold Rises Sharply Again; 415 Yuan Increase 62

Since this morning, each tael (ten taels), the initial opening benefited from the remaining momentum of the previous day, and with the foreign exchange rate weakening, people's hearts were even more firm. For a time, the buying interest on the trading floor was booming, and sellers disappeared. It leaped straight up, and the opening price at 9:30 was raised by 320 yuan. A money exchange firm bought 30 taels from a silver firm for 3,800 yuan. Then, a certain cash firm released a large amount of sales, and it soared another 50 yuan. A cash firm bought 20 taels from a certain bank for 3,850 yuan. Around 10 o'clock, a certain money exchange firm and silver firm suddenly started selling. At that time, the buying appetite seemed to weaken slightly, and the price immediately dropped by a small 100 yuan. A money exchange firm did 50 taels among themselves at a price of 3,750 yuan. Subsequently, it was heard that both the official and unofficial foreign exchange rates had shrunk, and a certain bank was making strong advances on behalf of outsiders, and retail investors were also entrusting brokers circulating in the market to absorb, which caused the market to turn upward suddenly and then soar by 270 yuan. A money exchange firm bought 20 taels from a silver firm for 4,020 yuan. After that, it was heard that the foreign exchange rate had eased, so most profit-taking parties rushed to sell at high prices. Except for a certain money exchange firm that had some buying appetite, the others were not very interested in buying, so the decline was also fierce. Before long, it plummeted by 210 yuan. Silver firms and cash firms sold 60 taels to a certain gold firm, all for 3,810 yuan. At noon, it rose slightly again. A money exchange firm bought 50 taels from a silver firm for 3,840 yuan. In the early afternoon, a silver firm sold a total of 50 taels to fellow firms and gold firms, all for 3,850 yuan. Later, because a certain bank made strong advances on behalf of customers, it soon raised the price by 90 yuan. A certain bank bought 10 taels from a gold firm for 3,940 yuan. At that time, silver firms took the opportunity to sell at high prices, and a certain gold firm also sold on behalf of out-of-town silver firms, which immediately caused a drop of 90 yuan. A silver firm sold 10 taels to a money exchange firm for 3,850 yuan. Later, the money exchange firm once again raised the price to 3,900 yuan, and then a silver firm sold 10 taels to a gold firm for 3,895 yuan, which was the closing price. As a result, it rose sharply by 415 yuan compared to the previous day, with fluctuations of 270 yuan throughout the day. The selling price of the cash firm's own brand of gold was 10 yuan higher than the spot gold price. The current standard gold price was 55 yuan lower than the listed gold price, and there were few transactions.

Jewelry Gold Listed High at 395 Yuan

Yarn and Cotton; Speculators Concentrate on the Yarn Market; Yarn Prices Soar 70

Double Horse and Heavenly Maiden Each Jumped 60 to 70 Yuan; Shenxin Factory Took the Opportunity to Open 3,000 Bales

The recent ups and downs in the spot yarn market have made people talk about tigers with fear. This situation is caused by the enthusiastic speculation of general speculators. However, real demand transactions are fearful and hesitant to move forward. According to market rumors, general speculators have made a large profit in the black market for foreign exchange and have already changed their course, and the wild fire has reignited in the cotton yarn market. Investigating the reasons for the upward trend: (1) the European war is fierce and foreign cotton is soaring; (2) the number of transport ships in the Far East is scarce, and cotton textiles are generally bullish, and a new buying trend is spreading, and market prices are soaring. It is found that the opening price of 20-count Double Horse yarn on Monday was only 570 yuan, and the high price today is 680 yuan, a huge jump of 110 yuan. As a result, it slightly eased back after closing. Shenxin Factory took the opportunity to open 3,000 bales of 20-count Double Horse at a price of 640 yuan, and the contract is scheduled to be padded with warehouse receipts at the end of this week. If the silver is not padded, the contract will be canceled, it is said.

The opening of spot yarn continued the remaining momentum from the previous day, rising by 5 yuan to 10 yuan. Subsequently, with the foreign exchange black market trending towards tightness, the buying interest continued to be strong, jumping another 30 yuan to 40 yuan. The spot price of 20-count Double Horse yarn rose directly from 630 yuan to 680 yuan, and the warehouse receipt price went directly from 600 yuan to 641 yuan. Other yarn brands also followed suit, but the momentum was more gradual. It is found that 1,295 bales were traded in half a day, but the actual sales were only 385 bales. The market price of 20-count Double Horse yarn rose by 73 yuan, Heavenly Maiden rose by 62 yuan, and Double Earth rose by 54 yuan. Today, there are a large number of cotton yarn exports, including 100 pieces shipped to Haikou, 20 pieces shipped to Beihai, 50 pieces shipped to Guangzhou Bay, 40 pieces shipped to Hong Kong, and 165 pieces shipped to Xiamen.
