Czech Nationals in China Eager to Serve England and France 76

Polish Consulate Notifies Nationals to Register for Military Service, British Ships Resume Voyages to the Far East, Departing Shanghai One After Another

With the outbreak of the European war, patriotic fervor has gripped foreign nationals residing in Shanghai, who are volunteering to fulfill their civic duty. Chinese citizens in this city, witnessing the hardships faced by the nation, express deep sympathy for the patriotism shown by these foreigners toward their homelands. In terms of maritime travel, there are reports that the British are considering providing naval escorts for ships sailing to Chinese ports, although the specific details remain unclear. A large batch of European mail arrived in Shanghai yesterday. Details regarding each situation are as follows:

Czech Nationals Submit Letter Volunteering

According to the English-language Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury, members of the Czech Association in Shanghai have sent identical letters to the British and French ambassadors to China. They state that as citizens of the Czech Republic, they are unaffected by the German invasion and are willing to serve the British and French governments. The full text of the letter is as follows:

"Your Excellency, we respectfully submit the resolution passed by a special meeting of the Czech Association in Shanghai. The resolution is as follows: At this perilous time when England and France have taken up arms to defend the most sacred and important human rights, the members of the Czech Association in Shanghai, representing 95% of the Czechs in China, feel it their duty to issue the following declaration for the information of all parties: (1) We still regard ourselves as citizens of the independent Czech Republic founded by the late President Masaryk. The Czech Republic has a constitution that embodies lofty principles, which were personified by the late President. Furthermore, we do not recognize as citizens of the Czech Republic those who have deemed it appropriate to exchange their original Czech passports for German ones. (2) Hitler's aggression and the so-called 'independence' of Slovakia have no impact on our legal status. We were citizens of the Czech Republic in the past, and we remain so now. (3) We solemnly declare that we fully sympathize with the democratic nations in this terrible war, which was not desired by democratic nations but has broken out. We are unanimously prepared to serve to the best of our abilities. Therefore, we unanimously await the disposition of the British and French authorities. If we receive orders from our national government specifying the extent of service, we will serve to that extent without reservation. The above resolution was proclaimed, discussed, and unanimously passed at a special meeting of the Czech Association in Shanghai on September 5th of this year and has been recorded in the association's journal. It has been signed by the members present at the special meeting. Respectfully submitted, Czech Association, Shanghai, September 5, 1939."

Polish Consulate Notifies Nationals to Enlist

According to the North-China Daily News, the Polish Consulate in Shanghai has notified Polish nationals in the city who wish to serve in the military to register with the consulate. It is reported that preparations are underway to arrange convenient transportation.

According to the Continental Daily News, reliable sources indicated last night (the 5th) that Polish residents in Shanghai will be given the opportunity to register with the Polish Consulate in Shanghai to join the military and will be provided with transportation back to Poland. However, the departure date has not yet been determined. The transportation may be via Canada. There are currently 400 Polish nationals in Shanghai. The Polish Minister to China, Mr. Woytowicz, will leave Shanghai on the Japanese Empress liner for Vancouver, from where he will return to his war-torn homeland. Mr. Bohomolec, the acting Polish Consul-General in Shanghai, will serve as Chargé d'Affaires at the Polish Legation here. The previous report that Mr. Bohomolec would leave Shanghai on the Empress liner was inaccurate.

Polish Envoy's Return Home Proceeding

Polish Minister to China, Mr. Woytowicz, having been ordered to return home to take up an important diplomatic post, left Shanghai on the 3rd with his wife and daughter aboard the Changxing Company's Japanese Empress liner. However, the ship had not been authorized by the British naval authorities and was therefore unable to sail. It is now learned that the Changxing Company obtained permission from the British Navy late the night before yesterday, and the ship departed Wusong immediately. After leaving Shanghai, Minister Woytowicz plans to travel to Vancouver, Canada, and then proceed to his new post. Yesterday's Western newspapers reported that the Polish Consul-General in Shanghai, Mr. Bohomolec, also returned home aboard the Changxing Company's liner, but this has been reported as inaccurate.

French Ambassador Hosts Banquet for French Nationals in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

The French Ambassador to China, Mr. Cosme, hosted a banquet yesterday afternoon at the Ambassador's residence on Haig Road for high-ranking French civil and military officials in Shanghai. Prominent French citizens were also invited to attend. It is reported that the French Ambassador made a statement regarding the current situation in Europe.

German Consul-General Notifies of Assumption of Office

The Shanghai Municipal Council recently received a notification stating that Mr. M. Fischer has been appointed as the German Consul-General in Shanghai and has taken over the German Consulate-General.

German Swastika Flags No Longer Seen

According to the North-China Daily News, although the French Concession authorities have not issued an order prohibiting the display of the German swastika flag, no swastika flags were seen in the French Concession yesterday (the 5th). It is believed that the German residents voluntarily removed these flags. German residents who previously wore Nazi party badges were also not wearing them yesterday. However, the German Consul-General in Shanghai has not issued any instructions regarding this matter.

Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation Refuses to Release German Funds

Mr. Hepburn, the manager of the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation, stated that the bank received a notification from the British Embassy that Britain and Germany are now formally at war, and diplomatic relations have been severed. According to item A of Article 3 of the notification, regarding the handling of matters such as loans and remittances involving the interests of enemy countries, the bank has been ordered to comply. Consequently, German merchants in England are no longer permitted to withdraw funds deposited in British banks. It is understood that regarding the deposits of Jewish refugees and Czech merchants in these British banks, some flexibility will be allowed due to the great hardships they have suffered.

Both Changxing Liners Depart for Hong Kong

The Changxing Company's steamships Japanese Empress and Asian Empress weighed anchor around 10 PM the night before last (the 5th) and departed for Hong Kong together. After arriving in Hong Kong, the Asian Empress will continue her original voyage to Manila. The Japanese Empress, which had arrived in Shanghai from Manila and Hong Kong, was supposed to proceed to Japan from Hong Kong and return to Vancouver via Honolulu. Unexpectedly, the ship departed for Hong Kong with the Asian Empress the night before last, heading directly to Honolulu and then returning to Vancouver without calling at Japan. The reason for this is unknown.

Italian Mail Increases Passenger and Freight Charges

The Italian mail ship Romolo Gessa, which had been delayed for several days, has been ordered to set sail by its head office after Italy declared its neutrality. The ship is scheduled to depart Shanghai on the 8th to return to Europe. The company believes that sailing under the current risky conditions warrants a reasonable price, so freight charges will be increased by 20% across the board, effective immediately. Passenger fares will increase by 40%. For example, the first-class fare from Shanghai to Hong Kong, previously £9 (British currency), will now be £12 and 12 shillings. The second-class fare, previously £6 and 8 pounds, will now be £8 and 8 shillings. The economic second-class (i.e., third-class) fare, previously £4, will now be £5 and 12 shillings. Fares to Southeast Asia and other foreign destinations will be increased by 40% across the board. The company's Conte Biancamano is still scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the 12th of this month.

British Mail Ships Permitted to Resume Voyages

The British Company's Elipoo arrived in Shanghai one day and was ordered to cease operations due to the situation. Now permission has been granted to set sail, and it is scheduled to leave the port at 6:00 AM this morning for Japan. Additionally, the Bengloe, which came from London, and the Nanking, which came from Australia, are both expected to arrive at the port at 3:00 PM today. The Bengloe will dock at the Qichang Wharf in Pudong, and the Nanking will dock at the Gonghexiang Wharf in Hongkou.

Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson Ships Depart

The ships of the British trading companies Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson, which operate along the Chinese coast, were previously ordered to suspend operations by the British Navy. As a result, all ships of both companies were completely suspended from service on the 1st of this week, creating a very tense situation. The situation gradually eased starting on Tuesday. Butterfield & Swire's Yisheng resumed service first, departing for Hong Kong on the afternoon of the 5th at 6:00 PM. The Zeh Sheng, Fu Sheng, Shun 犬, and other ships have since departed the port. Jardine Matheson's Tonghe, which operates on the Beisha Line, and Butterfield & Swire's Wulin departed simultaneously yesterday morning. The North and South Ocean Lines and the Haifang Line of both companies, as well as Butterfield & Swire's Shanghai-Tuidan and Singapore lines, have all resumed service on a scheduled basis and have now returned to the state they were in three days ago. The French Company's irregular ship Yangtsekiang arrived in Shanghai on the 5th and is scheduled to depart for Japan tomorrow (the 8th).

German Giant Liners Still Docked in Kobe

The German ships operating on the lower Yangtze River are still operating as usual. The Norddeutscher Lloyd's Scharnhorst, which is stranded in Kobe, was rumored yesterday to be leaving Japan for another destination. According to the company, this is not the case. Moreover, the sea is too dangerous for travel, so it will remain docked in Kobe with the Eider indefinitely. The Henck Company's Ramses is currently docked outside Wusong and has another ship in Japan, the name of which is unknown. The shipping industry has been shaken by the European situation for several days, but today it can be said to have temporarily stabilized. However, the future trend is still difficult to predict.

European Mail Arrives in Shanghai in Large Quantities

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency learned from the Transportation Section of the Postal Administration yesterday morning that the bureau is making every effort to facilitate mail delivery to and from European countries. A large batch of mail from Europe arrived on the Minis刁 liner at 11:00 AM yesterday, and a large batch of mail from Japan arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru in the afternoon. As for mail to be sent from Shanghai to European countries, (1) it will be carried by the 周列該撤 liner on September 7th, via the Suez Canal, arriving in London on October 5th; (2) it will be carried by the Kamakura Maru on September 15th, via the Pacific Ocean, arriving in London on October 17th. As for mail destined for Russia and Europe via Siberia, it will first be shipped to Tianjin or Qinhuangdao by steamer and then forwarded.

No One Delivering Overseas Parcels

Shipping between Shanghai and European countries has been interrupted, making postal delivery difficult and preventing the transport of commercial goods. Although the Shanghai Postal Administration is experiencing difficulties due to the disruption of international transportation, it is continuing to make efforts to facilitate postal delivery to Europe. In addition to regular, registered, and express mail, which are very congested, there is a clear lack of personnel to deliver large and small parcels destined for overseas destinations. Therefore, the business of the Postal Bureau's Overseas Parcel Section has come to a standstill.

Speculation Rampant, Foreign Exchange Plummets

The Shanghai foreign exchange black market yesterday's exchange rates, posted prices remained unchanged. However, actual market rates suddenly plummeted due to speculation. The British rate was 3 shillings 8.75 pence, and the US rate was 6.5 yuan. By 12:00 noon, bank buying rates were as follows: British rate 4 shillings, US rate 6.75 yuan, a decrease of 3,4375 compared to the previous five British rates, and a decrease of 5,625 British rates. As for the Central Bank's legal foreign exchange rates, they remained unchanged yesterday morning, with the British rate at 1 shilling 2.5 pence and the US rate at 20 US dollars. There was no market on Wednesday afternoon.

Foreign Currency Prices Have Already Soared

The Money Exchange Association announced the market buying and selling rates for its members. Yesterday morning, due to the contraction of the foreign exchange black market, foreign currency prices soared accordingly. The buying rate for US pounds was 81 yuan, and the selling rate was 85 yuan. The buying rate for British pound notes was 50 yuan and 50 cents, and the selling rate was 51 yuan and 50 cents. The buying rate for US pound was 84 yuan, and the selling rate was 88 yuan. The buying rate for US dollar notes was 13 yuan and 45 cents, and the selling rate was 13 yuan and 65 cents. The buying rate for Hong Kong notes was 3 yuan and 10 cents, and the selling rate was 3 yuan and 20 cents. There was still no market for German, French, and Italian currency.

The Securities Gray Market Has Stabilized

The securities gray market opened yesterday morning, and market sentiment has calmed down, with prices remaining very stable, without much fluctuation. The closing rates for yesterday afternoon are recorded below: Unified Public Bonds, Series A, 50 yuan and 4 cents; Series B, 43 yuan and 5 cents; Series C, 42 yuan and 5 cents; Series D, no transactions; Series E, 42 yuan and 25 cents.

Gold Prices Rise, Premium Slightly Increases

After opening yesterday morning, the gold gray market saw speculators rushing in due to the contraction of foreign exchange, causing market sentiment to rise and gold prices to rebound sharply. The closing price for the morning was 3,840 yuan, and the closing price for the afternoon was 3,900 yuan. The premium (exchange rate) was around 150 yuan. Saigon Rice Arrives in Shanghai Today 78

Preparing for Price Stabilization, Requesting Assistance from Authorities, Hoarders Take Advantage of Market Fluctuations

Mr. Yu Qiaqing previously noted that the supply of rice in Shanghai was disrupted, causing prices to soar and creating a serious situation. To alleviate the food shortage, he first ordered 18,000 bags of Saigon rice and, together with Mr. Li Fusun and Mr. Xu Jilu, telegraphed President Kong of the Executive Yuan, requesting the provision of foreign exchange. President Kong, concerned about the people's livelihood, immediately telegraphed back approving the purchase of £10,000 in foreign exchange at the official rate. The first batch of Saigon rice was shipped from Saigon on the 29th of last month aboard the Norwegian ship Haida, operated by the Wah Lun Shipping Company. A telegram has been received stating that the ship will arrive in Shanghai at 2:00 PM today (the 7th). Customs has been notified, and it is scheduled to dock at the Bund Wharf on Beijing Road for unloading. It is also learned that 500 tons of Saigon rice ordered by the British company Jardine Matheson were shipped to Shanghai aboard the French postal ship Chin La Sil. However, due to the outbreak of the European war, it was ordered to return after reaching the mouth of the Song River, preventing unloading. It is reported that the cargo owners will arrange for it to be reloaded onto a neutral country's ship and shipped to Shanghai again.

Cooperating with the Rice Industry to Stabilize Prices

Of the Saigon rice, 10,000 bags were ordered by the Refugee Relief Association and will be distributed to various shelters as food for refugees. The remaining 8,000 bags will be entrusted to rice industry organizations for distribution to various stores for price stabilization. The estimated price of the Saigon rice is over 30 yuan per stone. However, with the Ministry of Finance providing legal foreign exchange and granting tax-free imports, the cost per stone is only a little over 20 yuan, which will greatly benefit the common people. A meeting with rice industry organizations will be convened in the coming days to discuss price stabilization measures, and the Municipal Council will be asked to provide assistance.

Supply Lines Open, No Worries About Food

Regarding the registration of Saigon rice orders handled by the Accountants Association, yesterday saw the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital register for 250 bags and the Woolen Fabric Industry Association register for 250 bags. Including previous registrations, the total number has reached 4,786 bags. Various trade associations are currently handling registrations separately and will soon report the consolidated figures. The organizers will continue to place orders as soon as they have collected a sufficient number, and the rice will be transported on neutral country ships, unaffected by any obstacles. As for domestic rice, there has been a bumper harvest in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, and it has already entered the market one after another. Moreover, after the Municipal Council cleared the supply lines, there are no more problems. Therefore, a large amount of rice will be transported to Shanghai in the future, and there is no need to worry about food.

Recent Rice Prices Fluctuate

Although only 250 stone arrived in He Xia yesterday, hoarders released as many as 6,770 bags for sale. However, due to the impending arrival of Saigon rice and the price stabilization measures, rice shops were reluctant to buy, resulting in no interest in the morning market and a price drop of 1 yuan. However, after the afternoon opening, hoarders took the opportunity to manipulate prices, deliberately raising them, resulting in a rebound of 2 yuan. As a result, prices were actually 1 yuan higher than the previous day. Prices for glutinous rice also rose by 1 yuan due to scarcity.

Shanghai Citizens' Association Suggests Stamp Tokens 82

Readily Redeemable, Remedying the Difficulty of Small Change Shortage, To Be Terminated After the Government's Fractional Currency Notes Arrive in Shanghai

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association yesterday suggested that various public organizations promote "stamp tokens," readily redeemable, to facilitate commerce and industry, prevent the drawbacks of price vouchers, and remedy the difficulty of small change shortage. Details are as follows:

Suggesting the Promotion of Stamp Tokens

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association yesterday sent letters to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Bankers' Association, Shanghai Money Dealers' Association, Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession, and Cigarette Dealers' Association, stating: "Since the shortage of copper coins in this city, various industries have been using postage stamps as a substitute for small change. Recently, the Postal Administration has stated that it is difficult to recover the token stamps, and postage stamps have been rejected by the market. What has followed is the spontaneous price vouchers issued by various shops, which are diverse and plentiful, filling the market. The authenticity of these vouchers is mixed, and there are many drawbacks. The matter is sufficient to cause future troubles, which is very obvious. In order to facilitate commerce and industry and prevent losses to the public, this association has suggested the promotion of stamp tokens as a temporary remedy. We have long admired your association's enthusiasm for social welfare, and we have specially prepared a draft of the implementation measures for stamp tokens and the organizational outline of the stamp token management committee, each in one copy. We would like to ask for your valuable opinions. If you agree, we will schedule another meeting to discuss the matter. We hope you will consider and reply."

Implementation Measures for Stamp Tokens

(1) The issuance and redemption of stamp tokens shall be governed by these measures. (2) Stamp tokens shall be divided into two denominations: 1 cent and 2 cents. (3) A stamp token voucher shall be issued for stamp tokens. The voucher shall be made of cardboard, and in addition to the affixed stamp, it shall be sealed with transparent paper to prevent dirt and facilitate use. (4) The stamp token voucher shall be stamped by this association, and the voucher holder shall always keep the outer seal intact. (5) The redemption of stamp token vouchers shall be in legal tender, with the yuan as the unit. (6) The time for issuing and redeeming stamp token vouchers shall be from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM and from 1:00 PM to 4:00 PM daily. (7) The location for issuing and redeeming stamp token vouchers (to be determined later). (8) Stamp token vouchers shall be redeemed by this association for cash within one month after the government's fractional currency notes arrive.

Foreigners Register for Military Service, Municipal Council Sets Leave Procedures 84

Employees of Warring Nations Prohibited from Taking Long Leave, Resignations Must Be Submitted Six Months in Advance

The Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday (the 6th) issued a notice to its employees stating that all employees who are nationals of European warring nations are prohibited from taking military leave, and those who have already taken leave and left Shanghai will be suspended from their positions. Employees who are nationals of the United States, Japan, and other neutral countries may continue to work as usual and have the freedom to take long leave. According to Mr. Phillips, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Council, this measure is not related to financial considerations but is due to concerns that those who take long leave to return home may not be able to return to Shanghai on time due to the European war. It is also learned that employees who are nationals of warring nations such as Britain, Germany, and Poland, who resign from the council to join the volunteer forces of their respective countries, will still be approved, but the resignation must be submitted six months in advance, in accordance with the Municipal Council's established practice, and will only take effect after the full term. However, those who are

Military Reservists

who are recalled by their respective national governments will be given immediate approval by the Municipal Council to facilitate their immediate return home. In recent days, many British employees of the Municipal Council have registered for military service at the British Consulate. According to Mr. Phillips, the number of military reservists among them is relatively small. Mr. Phillips also stated that any council employee who returns home to serve in the military must

Resign According to Law

But their positions will still be given to them after they return to Shanghai. This is a way to take care of both emotions and reason. The Municipal Council is a municipal organization and must maintain its operations. If all employees were to leave their posts at this critical juncture, the council's affairs would inevitably be disrupted, as it would be very difficult to hire a large number of personnel to fill the vacancies here.

Several replies have been received, and the number of people to be investigated will increase to compile a reliable index table. The cost of living for Chinese workers continues to increase, with the total index at 234.17 (based on the average cost in 1936 as the base of 100), an increase of 45.61 compared to July, creating the

Highest record in the index table for the past four years

Comparing the classified indexes for July and August, food increased by 24.66%, clothing increased by 12.60%, fuel and lighting increased by 74.07%, and miscellaneous items increased by 24.69%. Since January of this year, the cost of living index has gradually increased, rising by 87.67% in eight months. One yuan of national currency in 1936 was still worth 6 jiao 7 fen 8 li at the end of last year, but last month it was

Worth only 4 jiao

2 fen 7 li. The reasons for the soaring cost of living can be summarized as follows: 1. Sharp contraction of foreign exchange; 2. Merchant manipulation; 3. The political situation makes people feel uneasy; 4. Transportation difficulties between rural and urban areas; 5. Sellers hoarding goods to seek huge profits, and buyers also hoarding goods to prevent shortages, resulting in ever-increasing prices; 6. Disappearance of copper coins, items that could be purchased with several copper coins or copper coins in the past are now priced in jiao coins.

Residents who purchase items piecemeal

Are greatly affected. Based on the above reasons, in the past few months, there have been dozens of items with price increases of more than 20%. August Industrial Report from the Public Works Department 90

Group training is effective, labor-management disputes are resolved

Although the prices of industrial raw materials in the city have increased, most factories were quite busy last month, except for a very few. There are a total of 46 silk reeling factories in this port, of which 30 are operating. However, the arrival of fresh lotus roots is not strong and is not enough to maintain long-term production. Four silk reeling factories with new equipment are able to reel high-quality lotus silk, which is actively sold abroad. The current situation of other silk factories is also good. Rubber shoe factories are experiencing business slump due to various reasons, such as the prohibition of transporting and selling sports shoes to neighboring provinces, rising raw material prices, and seasonal factors. Small-scale textile printing and dyeing factories have reduced work, but large-scale factories have been able to maintain their original production levels, except for a few that have reduced work. Flavoring powder factories are working well, but there is a shortage of gluten (a byproduct of starch), which is used as a raw material. Several waste cotton factories have temporarily stopped work, and straw weaving factories are also experiencing sluggish business. Last month, the new factories under preparation or already in operation that are worthy of attention include two silk factories and two chemical factories. A total of 165 factories were initially inspected by the Industrial Section.

Group training

On the 18th of last month, the Industrial Section held a lecture to explain how to start a fire to reduce smoke emissions. There were 138 boiler managers who attended the lecture. The "Industrial Common Sense and Safety Training Class" is scheduled to start on September 1st, with four hours of classes per week (completed in fifteen weeks). As of August 29th, a total of 118 trainees from registered factories have registered, including 31 boiler manufacturers and foremen. The manufacturers of small light bulbs held a meeting to continue discussing business standards. Leather factory owners held two meetings successively. In addition, the Hot Water Bottle Factory Association also held a meeting. At that time, the association invited a representative from the Industrial Section to attend the meeting and provide instructions on the safe prevention methods for using celluloid paint.

Boiler management

Last month, 80 boilers that had not been registered before were applied for registration by the factory owners. The factory owners submitted 35 installation inspection certificates and 9 annual inspection certificates. Three more registered boiler manufacturers were added last month, bringing the total to 15. One of the newly registered ones is located in the Eastern District. A boiler manufacturer, despite repeated warnings, still failed to hire a qualified engineer to inspect the products, and the boiler plates used did not meet the required conditions. Therefore, the court has issued a summons and scheduled a hearing. The number of boilers sealed by the Public Works Department has increased by 95, bringing the total to 220.

Accidents

A total of 192 accidents were reported, including 11 fatalities. A total of 21 women were injured. The exact causes of the accidents are known in 185 cases. 61 cases have been thoroughly investigated and the factory has been ordered to adopt preventive measures. According to the classification of causes, accidents caused by machines driven by mechanical force were the most common, with a total of 32 cases, of which 12 cases were related to belts and gears. There were 7 cases caused by electricity, including 3 fatalities. A total of 7 workers were injured in explosions, including 1 death. According to the industrial classification, the most accidents occurred in the textile industry, including 3 fatalities. A total of 7 fires occurred in factories, injuring 3 workers, but no one died.

Labor disputes

The Industrial Section handled a total of 9 labor disputes, of which 5 were caused by requests for wage increases. As a result, the section assisted in resolving them. Several factories and businesses, in view of the increasing cost of living, have increased the treatment of workers. In the past two months, many factories have increased wages twice. However, whether the percentage of wage increases is sufficient to cover the increased percentage of living expenses.

Cao actually presented the forged reconciliation document to the court as an excuse. Later, Cai commissioned the China Recording Company to collect Cao's confession of the crime from the telephone in order to seek collateral evidence. Cao and Cai admitted in Shanghai dialect that they had stolen Cai's seal, so Cai made the recording into a record and commissioned lawyer Xu Jinyu to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court against Cao for the crime of forging documents, and presented the record as strong collateral evidence. Cao then hired lawyer Huang Zengjie to defend him and filed a counterclaim against Cai for false accusation. The court, according to the complaint, after repeated trials by Judge Sun Pengxian, at the end of last month

Declared the end. Judge Yu ordered Cao to pay a shop deposit of 1,000 yuan and be released pending sentencing. Yesterday was the date of sentencing. Judge Sun took the bench in Criminal Court 2 and announced the judgment: Cao Wenyu's forgery of documents was sufficient to harm others, and he was sentenced to six months of imprisonment, but considering that he was a first-time offender, he was granted a three-year reprieve. Regarding Cao Wenyu's counterclaim against Cai Xiaoti for false accusation, Cai Xiaoti was innocent. After Cai received the judgment, because the civil part was suspended for trial, now that the criminal part has come to an end, he decided to apply to the civil court judge to continue the trial.

Education News

Ministry of Education Revises Wartime Book and Magazine Review Regulations 102

Instructing All Provincial Education Departments to Comply

(Chongqing Dispatch) The Ministry of Education has revised the "Wartime Book and Magazine Review Regulations" and issued a circular to all provincial education departments to comply and implement. The details of the regulations are as follows: (1) During the War of Resistance, in order to meet wartime needs and unify national thought, the central government has established the Central Book and Magazine Review Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Central Review Authority) to adopt a manuscript review method to handle all review matters related to books and magazines. (2) The Central Review Authority shall be jointly organized by the Propaganda Department of the Central Executive Committee, the Political Department of the Military Affairs Commission, the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Education, and the Central Social Department, and shall be the highest book and magazine review authority in the country. Its organizational outline will be determined separately. (3) If there are differences of opinion regarding the review of books and magazines by the Central Review Authority, the opinion of the representative of the Central Propaganda Department shall prevail. (4) To facilitate the rapid publication of books and magazines in various regions, local book and magazine review committees (hereinafter referred to as Local Review Authorities) shall be established under the guidance of party, government, military, and police agencies in major cities (or provincial capitals) to handle the review of books and magazines in their respective jurisdictions. Establishment is not permitted if there are few bookstores and publishing houses in the area. The general rules for the organization of the Local Review Authorities will be determined separately. (5) When reviewing various books and magazines, if the Local Review Authorities discover major errors, they should order the suspension of printing, or if the content is complex and cannot be decided independently, they should submit the original manuscript along with a signed opinion to the Central Review Authority for approval before implementation. As for books and periodicals that should be revised or abridged, the Local Review Authorities may handle them independently, but must promptly report them to the Central Review Authority for record. (6) Bookstores and publishing houses in various regions must submit books and magazines for review and approval by the review authority in their location before they are allowed to be published, with the exception of natural sciences and applied sciences unrelated to national defense, and textbooks for primary, secondary, and vocational schools, and mass education schools, which should be submitted to the Ministry of Education for review. If there is no Local Review Authority in the location, they may submit them directly to the Central Review Authority. Purely academic works that do not involve current affairs, political, social, or ideological issues may not be required to submit the original manuscript for review, but they must be submitted to the review authority for review before publication. (7) After publication by our Party and various military and political agencies, one copy must be submitted to the Central Review Authority for record. (8) When bookstores and publishing houses submit books and magazines for review, they must submit one copy of the original manuscript or two copies of the proof. After the Local Review Authority completes the review and if there are no inappropriate contents, the original manuscript or proof will be stamped with a "Reviewed" seal and returned to the submitter. (9) If the opinions in the submitted book or magazine manuscript are completely erroneous, the process will be stopped. If a portion is erroneous, it must be revised or deleted according to the indicated points before publication is allowed. (10) For books and magazines that have been reviewed by the review authority, two copies must be submitted to the respective review authority for re-examination before they are allowed to be published. (11) For books and magazines that have been approved for publication by the review authority, except as otherwise provided in Articles 6 and 7, or if the review authority does not allow publication, or if they are published without authorization without complying with the indicated revisions or deletions, they will be confiscated and punished. Those with reactionary arguments may also be punished in accordance with the revised Publishing Law for their editors, printers, or publishers. (12) Books and magazines submitted for review that have a correct attitude, excellent content, and are beneficial to the War of Resistance may be rewarded separately. The measures will be determined separately. (13) Books and magazines approved for publication by the review authority will be issued a review certificate. The review certificate number should be printed in No. 5 lead type in the lower corner of the cover of the book or magazine for verification. Those that are printed without a review certificate or fraudulently printed will be subject to heavier penalties in accordance with the provisions of Article 11. (14) The review time for books and magazines: no more than five days for books within 100,000 words, no more than ten days for books over 100,000 words, no more than five days for quarterly magazines, no more than two or three days for semi-monthly and monthly magazines, and no more than one day for weekly and ten-day magazines. This limit does not apply if the content is erroneous and needs to be submitted for verification. (15) If the Central Review Authority considers that the Local Review Authority has handled matters inappropriately, it may order rectification at any time. (16) If the submitting bookstore or publishing house considers that the Local Review Authority has handled matters inappropriately, it may state the reasons and request a review, and may also request that it be forwarded to the Central Review Authority for review. (17) The review standards for books and magazines shall be handled in accordance with the revised "Review Standards for Books and Magazines during the War of Resistance." (18) Before these regulations are implemented, books and magazines that have already been published will still be subject to post-publication review, in accordance with the "Measures for Inspecting Bookstores Selling Prohibited Publications" and the "Provisional Measures for Reviewing, Banning, and Unbanning Books and Magazines." (19) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the Propaganda Department, the Social Department, and the political, internal affairs, and education departments may consult and revise them. (20) These regulations shall be decided by the Propaganda Department, Social Department, Political Department, Ministry of Interior, and Ministry of Education, and shall be implemented after being submitted to and approved by the Standing Committee of the Central Executive Committee, and shall be submitted to the Military Affairs Commission and the Executive Yuan for record.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Sends Condolences to Wu Zhiqian 103

Chongqing, June 6th. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek sent a telegram to Minister Chen of the Education Department, saying: "Minister Chen of the Education Department, I am saddened to learn from the reports that Wu Zhiqian, the principal of Shanghai Women's University, was murdered for refusing to collaborate with the enemy. This is important. Chiang Kai-shek, Yu Shi Mi Yu."

Free Talk

Time 112

— Hong Kuangcheng

——To a friend who trusts me

What makes you live? It's time that never stops for a second. Time and life are fused together, they stand on the same track, pushing life forward. But time has a strange "temper" that surprises you. You must satisfy it, it can give you a valuable life, give you a beautiful life. Otherwise, it will turn you into an outdated person.

I can tell you about its "temper", that is: what most people dislike makes it like, and what most people are satisfied with makes it unhappy. For example, on this hot day, you work hard, and the stench of sweat makes people sick, which can gain the favor of time, it will reward your diligence. If you are surrounded by air conditioning, singing and dancing with glamorous people, and the strong fragrance of powder fills the air, even if you think this is beautiful, time hates these, it will punish you, block your path to light, and soon you will be at a crossroads, hesitating.

What I said is not fabricated out of thin air, using illusory statements to confuse you. This is the experience of countless people, the conclusion drawn from the practice of countless people.

Time gives people a serious life, creates an era for mankind, forward, great...

When time pushes the era, it is faster than anything else, you must make good use of the time that belongs to you, you cannot neglect to let it slip from your fingers, ears, and eyes. You have to grab it and run with it. You should not wait for your companions to urge you and encourage you. If you are not careful and slack off a little, in an instant, you have fallen behind!

I sincerely advise you, do not use fantasy or empty hope as materials to fill your time. You should do it practically, grasp the forward life, and overcome all difficulties.

Please don't be complacent, thinking that you have made sufficient use of your time, and admit that you have stepped up your pace in the forward horn. You should examine, what are the shortcomings, regarding time; what else is there to be hidden. Based on your introspection, transform your life again!

My words are not the most brilliant, they can only be used as some reference in life. In the process of your forward life, I hope you can write a page that is more valuable than this.

The Confessions of a Spanish Refugee (Part 2) 113

— Written by Marcelino Sunhi of Spain, translated by Wang Fen

I put my shoes back on, then put on my bathrobe, and wrapped myself in a blanket, and went to bed horizontally. My pillow was a cheap cardboard bag. It wasn't soft, but it was comfortable enough.

I didn't know what time it was when the sound of torrential rain woke me up. The blanket and clothes on my body were still wrapped tightly, but soon I felt raindrops flowing down from above, passing through my abdomen and flowing straight down. The water droplets were already warm when they flowed there. I could handle it. Later I made a trough on my back, but unexpectedly there was water flowing between my legs again. There were puddles of water all around me, and the puddles were all warmed by my body. I didn't dare to move my body, for fear of splashing the puddles open, but slowly I felt unbearably cold. I wanted to find a tent where I could hide from the heavy rain. But they were all crowded with people, so I could only slowly turn around and look for the shelter in the sand cave.

Saint. Xuepolin was already overcrowded. As many as 60,000 refugees were stationed there. The death rate was probably fifteen people per day, and we felt lucky, because Daoli had no sanitation facilities or medical equipment. I talked to a French officer about it. But he comforted me:

'You Spaniards are really hardy...! When we imprison the Germans in the camp, sixty of them die every day. I don't understand. Your death rate is only fifteen people per day. It's amazing!'

We were so dissatisfied with him, we were really sorry. Maybe he hoped that the vicious "red elements" would die six hundred a day, so that the problem of France could be solved. Unfortunately, the Germans have very sophisticated camps.

He had no relatives anywhere. No one in the world would write him a short letter of sympathy. Yet morning and night, he would always go to the post office - the camp post office - and ask: Is there any mail for Manuel Espinilla? He knew that the answer would be no. Yet he had to ask! How terrible it is to feel alone in a crowd! But later he broke the rules. He actually wrote a letter to me in England:

"Can you write me a letter? Every day I go to the post office and always get the same answer: no letter from you, Espinilla. I know that I have no relatives in the world, and although you are also a prisoner in a hellish camp, you know how much comfort letters can give to our companions, please write me a letter!"

I did write back to him. And we are still corresponding. I think this is a human obligation.

Aim 114

Anchoring at Night 115

— Zhenghua

The setting sun sank below the horizon, and the shadows of crows in the distant sky also disappeared into the vast clouds and trees. The twilight gradually thickened and spread out; the uneven shadows of sails became as dim and hazy as gray clouds.

The gentle sound of oars rippled slightly in the clear blue waves. The water splashed by the bamboo pole slightly moistened the corners of my sleeves. The water flowed very slowly and loosely; like a tired snake struggling to wriggle, duckweed rippled out circles of grain, the large circles expanded to the shore and disappeared, and the small circles expanded again.

Our boat was rowed to the riverbank of × village and anchored. Dense green shade covered both sides of the bank. A gentle wind swayed the willow branches and slanted into the cabin, lightly stroking my disheveled hair. The croaking of frogs in the fields was like a gust of wind, creating a messy sound like rain; clear shepherd songs floated in the twilight; the varying degrees of these two sounds seemed very discordant. Deep in the muddy road on the bank were the marks of hooves and straw sandals. The shadows of farmers in bamboo hats were still moving in the distance, and finally disappeared into the green gauze curtain. A wisp of cooking smoke circled over the uneven thatched roofs, slowly merging with the floating clouds.

I had dinner on the boat, rested for a while, then climbed out of the cabin, and treading on the clear moonlight, prepared to make a tour of this quiet village. × Village belongs to the occupied × County. Harbors crisscross around it, but the area is very secluded, and the iron hooves of the enemy have not yet trampled it. — I thought so on the road.

Cows lay obliquely under the pine trees, their noses twitching, sighing. Dogs curled up on the woodpile, and seeing a stranger, they didn't bark loudly, but slowly stood up and smelled the corners of his clothes. Children were rolling and laughing in the square. Farmers were holding dry tobacco bags and sitting leisurely under the bean trellis, chatting about the abundance of the harvest, with relaxed smiles on everyone's faces.

A surprised look swept over my face.

"Eh - sir, it's so late, where are you from?"

"I came by boat from ××"

"Is the county seat lost?"

"This is absolutely true, the county seat has long been lost -"

Many people surrounded me.

"Our county seat is lost, we are waiting for the opponents to come -"

"Our army fought fiercely in Qingjiang. After Qingjiang was lost, the county seat here was no longer important in terms of military situation, so it was evacuated. - I explained excitedly, I looked at them.

"Our home is here, if they want to come, they have to fight!

I briefly explained the situation of the war again, they became calm, the people surrounding me became thicker, but I became more excited. I stared at these simple farmers, the hot blood of defending their hometown was surging in them, they were all deep in thought...

I went back to the boat with a slightly heavy step, sat by the window, staring at the undulating waves. Moonlight, starlight and lamplight were all reflected in the water, swaying, sometimes merging into one piece, sometimes rippling into thousands of points.

"The tide is rising!" The boatman shouted loudly.

I quietly listened to the sound of the tide gently flowing, and let the moonlight gently kiss my forehead. At this time, many images of simple farmers also poured out in my heart. They were all calm, very calm...

Unrecognized People 116

— Mu Jie

While illiteracy is a serious problem, it's not the end of the world; but if you can't recognize people, don't even think about making a life for yourself!

The world is inherently a place where people interact with each other. To make your way in life, you have to mingle among people! But among the teeming masses, there are those who are wise, foolish, virtuous, and unscrupulous. If you're fortunate enough to encounter only the wise and virtuous, you can live a carefree and contented life; but if you unfortunately find yourself among the foolish and unscrupulous, you'll live a wretched life, causing endless harm.

Recognizing characters seems difficult, but it's actually not. Recognizing people seems easy, but it's actually not.

"Judging by appearances" inevitably leads to "missing out on Ziyu." Most fortune-tellers claim to be immortals or semi-immortals, saying they can know everything about a person in detail. This is their professional way of recognizing people; the speaker may be speaking casually, and the listener can take it with a grain of salt. As for someone like Lord Pingyuan, who seemed to be good at assessing talented people, he still missed Mao Sui. So to recognize people, you need "great discernment." As for me, I'm often confused, or even recognize people without truly knowing them, which can lead to endless trouble.

When you meet someone, you must first discern their character: are they a superior person? Or an inferior one? Are they good? Or evil? Are they learned? Or uneducated? Are they easy to deal with? Or difficult? Examine them carefully, recognize them clearly, and then deal with them appropriately. This is the general way to conduct oneself in the world. As for me, if I misjudge someone and offend them, not only might I get a slap in the face, but I might also be lectured, "Friend! Open your eyes and see clearly, who am I?" At that time, I'd be suffering the consequences of my own actions, asking for trouble, not only failing to recognize the person, but also lacking social awareness.

When making friends, you also need to recognize people; it's best to stay far away from cliques of rogues. But sometimes you also need to be careful and thoroughly understand the other person; otherwise, you might make the mistake of "befriending the wrong person" or "marrying the wrong partner." And you might even be "sold out by a friend for personal gain" or have a friend "kidnapped."

However, as the world gets worse, recognizing people becomes even more difficult. Fortune-tellers claim to have an iron tongue, but they actually have a honeyed tongue. As for assessing a person, it's also quite difficult; a slight mistake can lead to "a difference of a thousand miles," even if it's only "an error of a hair's breadth." When it comes to making friends, it's even more difficult. Sometimes you might even know that the other person is not good, but because of vested interests, or being threatened or tempted, you disregard everything and treat them as a close friend, the result of which is naturally unimaginable.

If you don't use accurate judgment, but rely on arrogance, misjudging the other person, thinking they're not worth striking at, and assuming you can make your own plans and secure victory, this kind of failure to recognize people will naturally only lead to sinking deeper and deeper into the mire, until you can't extricate yourself.

If, for the sake of temporary interests, you jointly enter into some agreement with a country that is fundamentally incompatible, treating it as a close friend, thinking you can achieve "cooperation," this kind of failure to recognize "people" will naturally end with being sold out by a friend.

Therefore, recognizing people seems easy, but it's actually not. For individuals, if you don't recognize people, you're bound to suffer for life; for a country, if you don't recognize "people," its own people will inevitably live in poverty, and the day of its collapse will be closer.

Arts and Entertainment World

Bai Xue Yang Chun, Guangling Jue Xiang, A Brief Account of the People of the Xian Ni Society 117

— Mei Xiang Shi Zhu

The stories of Kunqu opera are mostly adapted from various legends, and eight out of ten are from "Zhui Bai Qiu." Most of the southern tunes are also from the Jiangsu and Zhejiang regions, such as the "Yong Tuan Yuan," which some say is based on real events in Tangqi, and the lyrics and dialogue are mostly in the Suzhou dialect. Now, the actors of the Xian Ni Society are all from Suzhou, and their skills are refined, so they should all reach the realm of transformation. Those who understand the art praise them for transforming the customs and correcting the elegance. However, the "family troupe" has been swaying in the wind and rain for more than ten years, and only a few remain, and even the flute players are as rare as morning stars. In addition to drinking and tapping the clapper, I will briefly record the actors' skills, adding flowers to the brocade. If there is anything inappropriate, I hope those who know will correct it.

Zhu Chuanming

Studies the role of Dan. Has a beautiful appearance, clear and gentle voice, and graceful stage presence. Recently, her voice has become even sweeter and mellower. Her interpretation of Gui Zhi in "Selling Horses" is more delicate and considerate. She is capable in many plays, and "Wandering in the Garden, Startled by a Dream," "Breaking the Willow, Yangguan," "Need for Vinegar," and "Zhao Jun Goes Beyond the Border" are her best works.

Zhang Chuanfang

Charming and flirtatious, her interpretations of "Good Date," "Thinking of the Mortal World," "Qin Pick," and "Stealing Poetry" are all witty and flavorful. Her pronunciation is clear and resonant. When she plays Fei Gongren in "Assassinating the Tiger," she is praised by music experts. She is both bold and chivalrous, and chivalrous and sad. She is amiable and has no airs of a star.

Zheng Chuanjian

Studies phonology diligently. Capable of playing Sheng, Wai, and Lai roles. Her portrayal of Li Guinian in "Tan Ci" exudes a sense of desolation and loss in her eyes, which even painters cannot capture.

Zhou Chuanying

Courteous and refined, is a talented Xiaosheng actor. His portrayal of Pan Bizheng in "The Jade Hairpin" surpasses the characters in paintings. It is said that his performance as Li Hongji in "Fighting with Knives" is extremely wonderful, but I have not had the opportunity to see it. I once saw him play Que Zhong in "What Can Be Done," and his demeanor was dignified and handsome.

Zhao Chuanqun

Has a gifted voice. Her performances in "Pipa" and "Jingchai" are like writing the "Huangting Sutra" for the first time, just right. Her interpretation of "Selling Horses" is also a masterpiece. It is better for her to not wear a beard when playing male roles.

Fang Chuanyun

Her martial arts skills have greatly improved recently. Her pronunciation is clear and round. Her portrayal of Zidan in "Sending Her Son" is extremely difficult to sing, but she can achieve perfection. "San Cha Kou," "Qianyuan Mountain," "Lin Chong Flees in the Night," and "Flaming Mountain" are all her specialties. Her appearance is very much like a young girl.

Wang Chuanqian

An outstanding Wusheng actor. His performance of "Ji Qin San Dang" is his signature. Recently, he has not been able to perform it due to the lack of supporting actors. "An Tian Hui," "Ning Wu Guan," and "Song Shi Hui" emphasize both singing and acting. Every time he goes on stage, he is willing to put in effort, and his every move is very standardized.

Shen Chuanyin

The most respected big painted face in the Kunqu troupe. Chuankun is from a theatrical family. His performances of "Fire Judge," "Marrying a Sister," and red-faced plays all have the right measure. At a time when dharma music is declining, there is no one to follow in his footsteps with such talent.

Zhang Chuanfang's "Assassinating the Tiger" 118

New Film Introduction

"The Man in the Iron Mask" 119

— Qi Hua

"The Man in the Iron Mask" has always been a mystery in history. Although there are many books of research by later generations, there is no definitive "search for hidden meaning." Alexandre Dumas's "The Man in the Iron Mask" is a sequel to "The Three Musketeers." His focus is on praising the Three Musketeers for their loyalty and service to the country, and not on seeking the truth about the Man in the Iron Mask. However, this legendary story reflects the obscenity of the royal palace and the cruelty of Louis. The main cause of the later French Revolution was the resistance aroused by Louis's harsh taxes and tyrannical punishments.

As a historical film, "The Man in the Iron Mask" is directed with considerable skill. He delicately writes about the two aspects of strength and mercy between Louis XIV and Philippe. For example, Louis's heavy use of the treacherous minister Fouquet and his favoritism towards the noblewoman Madame de la Vallière led to widespread resentment. When Louis was about to arrive at the church to pray, he was ambushed. When Philippe wore the royal robes and went to the church in his place, he asked about the suffering of the people and comforted them with great care, and the people shouted long live. This powerful contrast makes people deeply moved by the fact that a tyrannical ruler is bound to be overthrown one day.

Louis Hayward, who plays Louis XIV and Philippe, also gives an excellent performance. Louis's treachery and cruelty, and Philippe's bravery and vitality, are deeply portrayed in both their actions and voices, creating two absolutely different characters.

What is regrettable is that the development of the first half of the play is too calm, although the individual scenes are commendable. The second half, after Philippe is imprisoned wearing an iron mask, and Louis XIV is lured into prison by the Three Musketeers, is the most exciting scene in the whole film, with the prisoners shouting, Louis promising wealth to the jailer, and the jailer whipping him while laughing. In the end, Philippe marries Princess Marie, Fouquet informs, and the Three Musketeers die heroically. D'Artagnan also dies with a smile beside Philippe after the ceremony, which is deeply moving.

The cinematography is very beautiful, such as the shot of Louis XIV looking down at the carriage from the upstairs, the composition is very novel and beautiful; the reflection of the river light when the Three Musketeers travel in the tunnel, and the gloom in the prison are all very beautiful.

Anecdotes from the Pear Garden 120

— Xu Muyun

The people in the opera troupe are extremely lacking in ethics, (meaning they are lacking in virtue and shameless). Later, that brilliant old man gave these low-level opera busybodies who take kickbacks another nickname, calling them "eating flyers." Since the name has been determined, they can write in the accounts in large letters, "Paid the 'eating flyers' several yuan and several cents." The most unfortunate thing is that these people also carry the sign of a critic and often appear in newspapers. But in reality, except for a very few three or five people, the rest of the Ping opera critics in Beiping are looked down upon by the actors.

These two kinds of people have not yet been discovered in Shanghai. Although there are many people who love drama and criticize drama, the first thing is that they never watch free shows; the second thing is that all the Pingjiao who come to Shanghai must fulfill their "traveling guest visiting resident guest" etiquette. To pay a visit, they have to spend money to treat guests and reserve seats. Not only has no one ever eaten the actors, but they have all taken out money to spend on them. Sometimes the theater helps them publish special collections and special issues, and they have to write articles for them for free. The actors and theater authorities use the Shanghai Ping opera critics to do voluntary publicity and support, but the Ping opera critics never ask them to sing at the dinner table. The Da Jiao who come south from Ping also know that the real Ping opera critics are completely different from the "opera busybodies" and "eating flyers" of Beiping. I think all Ping opera critics should continue to maintain this honor and not allow the northern wind to gradually spread south. This is the glory of the entire Ping opera circle in Shanghai. If there are one or two unscrupulous people who follow famous actors day and night, or have the idea of eating actors, then the two dishonorable titles of "opera busybody" and "eating flyer" will immediately be added to the bodies of Shanghai Ping opera critics by the actors. I hope this does not happen, and I hope it never happens. This is the glory of the entire Ping opera circle in the isolated island. (94)

Interesting Stories from Film City

Dance Instructor Loudly Appeals to Actresses Not to Neglect Leg Beauty 121

— Feng Xiang

Le Roy Prinz, the dance instructor expert at Hollywood's Paramount Pictures, also critiques women's beautiful legs. In the past six years, he has inspected more than 5,000 pairs, but he considers few of them satisfactory. Therefore, he has to stand up and loudly appeal, warning women, especially actresses, not to neglect the beauty of their legs any longer.

Prinz says that if women could devote half the time they spend on decorating their faces to paying attention to their legs, the world would definitely produce a few more beauties. According to his statistics, only about 5% of women pay attention to their legs.

Recently, Paramount Pictures plans to shoot a film called "Million Dollar Legs." Prinz selected an actress named Betty Grable, feeling that her leg beauty is the best among Hollywood stars and worthy of playing the protagonist in this film. It is said that Miss Betty has had healthy and beautiful legs like other girls since she was a child, but because she didn't just know how to apply nail polish and draw eyebrows when she grew up, she was also able to pay attention to her legs at the same time, wearing matching high heels, walking in a regular gait, and performing appropriate muscle-developing exercises, so she has been able to maintain the beauty of her powder legs.
